<Review>I'm sorry to say not good. I have been in Manteca since 1984. This place has been an Italian restaurant the entire time. We loved it when it was Pietros enjoyed it when it was Dave and Sylvia's. During this time Manteca obtained many more options and the restaurant in the Cardoza Center fell off our radar. We were in the neighborhood looking for a place to eat and decided to give Angelenos a try. We both had pasta dishes Chicken Parmesan for myself Shrimp and scallops Alfredo. The chicken was not pounded and the sauce had no flavor. My dish again flavorless and completely lacked the richness you'd expect from an Alfredo sauce. The decor is exactly the same and was out dated in the early 80s. Our server was attentive enough since we were the only ones in there but he was dressed in Jeans, flannel shirt and a baseball style hat. We probably will not be back.< /Review>< user_id>

<userid>106492645185947610764< /userid><Text>So, for years, I have been dealing with drop foot and a callus, or what I thought was a "tailor's" bunion, that had moved in under the pad of my small toe. Every step I took felt like I was stepping on a sharp object. Custom insoles, orthotics, pain medications, lotions and creams provided some relief, but the pain always returned within a day or two - sometimes within hours. Now, sixteen weeks after back surgery to address my drop foot, my gait has improved along with the redistribution of weight towards my big toe. However, the pain under my small toe pad has remained. That was until I saw Dr. Hejat. After a Q&A consult, he took a look at my foot and quickly identified a thickened callus that was the cause of my pain. After gently removing it, he moved on to my shoe insole. He noticed I was using a "ball of foot" gel pad as a cushion and quickly cut a pressure-free relief zone out of the gel pad before reinserting the insole into my shoe. After putting my shoes back on I took a few steps and was completely pain free! No surgery, no injections, and no up sale or talk of needing custom orthotics or insoles. From beginning to end, check-in to walk-out, a great experience and an even better result!</Text>< Response>

<Rate>4<//Rate>< Review>
We stopped here during our self guided hike tour & the customer service was amazing! My favourite part was the wine tasting at the tasting bar which was just $10 for 5 different wines! I also loved my salted caramel with nuts ice cream. Very rich & appropriate after a long bike ride. The only downside was my spinach ravioli. There was barely any seasoning or flavouring. We went here on a Saturday afternoon and it wasnâ€™t even packed. Made it the perfect pit stop. We ended up covering it in pepper to make it taste better. Other than the ravioli, everything was great!<//Review>

<UserId.>111991419067732910868</UserId.><GmapID>0x808fbb1b337705ed:0x256f46dde09c04b8<//GmapID><username>Diana Griffin<//username><Rating>5< /Rating></record>

1594225424424</date>
< rating>
4</rating>
< Text>
Long time community resource, now under private management.  Like many community pools, this is primarily used by Palo Alto residents, but is open to all (residents get a modest discount for some, but not all usage).

This is also the largest site for one of the bigger age group competitive swim clubs, Palo Alto Stanford Aquatics, who use the 25 yard pool year round for practices for enrolled athletes from 5-6 year olds, all the way to college swimmers on break, and the occasional professional swimmer.

The pool is nestled in Rinconada Park, a sparsely developed space in the heard of residential Palo Alto.  Consisting mostly of open space, tennis courts, a newly built fire station, and the local public elementary school, this is always a pleasant area top stop by.

There is also a substantial community center and library on either side of the park, so anyone that lives locally is likely to visit this location for a variety of purposes, and having the pool here just gives you another reason to treat yourself to a little pool time.< /Text>

< Review>
Given that this is the only Old Navy store in the city, the store has a wide variety of products. I believe they have everything old navy offers. The service is fine, pretty much what you'd expect from an Old Navy, you have to go up to the sales associates if you need anything tho some of them might come up to you and check it. On the register sometimes might be a line but the check out process doesn't take long as there are always plenty of people on the registers. Getting here is easy as it is located on market street and right next to the Powell street station, Don't ever think about driving here tho. Overall a nice store experience.</Review>
